Euclid's Angle Bisection Against the Indivisible Part
Al-Jurjani presents Euclid's proof that angles are infinitely divisible, negating the indivisible part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Euclid's geometric proof of infinite angle bisection demonstrates the non-existence of an indivisible part of magnitude.

Core Idea
Infinite bisectability of angles disproves the atomistic indivisible part.

This lesson presents the fifth proof from Euclid's Elements against the doctrine of the indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajazza). Using elementary geometry, Euclid shows that any rectilinear angle can be bisected repeatedly without end, implying that spatial magnitudes are infinitely divisible. This conclusion challenges the atomistic view held by some kalām theologians.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once. Then read the English translation. Notice that the proof is presented as a concise logical progression.
The passage is dense; reading it twice helps.
2
Trace the logical steps
Identify the key claim: any rectilinear angle can be bisected. Its half is also a rectilinear angle that can be bisected, and so on. This leads to infinite divisibility.
This is a straightforward geometric demonstration.
3
Connect to the conclusion
Understand why infinite divisibility negates the 'part' (al-juz'). If an angle can be divided infinitely, no smallest indivisible unit exists. This refutes the atomistic view of space.
The proof uses geometry but has ontological implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه (الخامس: برهن إقليدس) في المقالة الأولى من كتاب الأصول ( أن الزاوية المستقيمة الخطين قابلة للتنصيف بخط مستقيم فيكون نصفها زاوية مستقيمة الخطين قابلة للتنصيف أيضاً، وهكذا فالزاوية المستقيمة الخطين (تنقسم إلى غير النهاية، وأنه ينفي الجزء ) .
The fifth proof: Euclid proved in the first article of the Book of Elements that the rectilinear angle is capable of being bisected by a straight line, so its half is also a rectilinear angle capable of being bisected, and so on. Thus the rectilinear angle divides infinitely, and this negates the part.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage states the fifth proof (al-wajh al-khamis) against the indivisible part, drawn from Euclid's Elements, Book I. Euclid demonstrated that any rectilinear angle can be bisected by a straight line, and the resulting half is itself a rectilinear angle that can be bisected again, ad infinitum. This infinite divisibility of a finite angle shows that there is no smallest, indivisible part of spatial magnitude. The proof directly refutes the atomistic doctrine that space is composed of discrete, indivisible units.

Key Terms
الزاوية المستقيمة الخطين
التنصيف
غير النهاية
الجزء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Euclid's angle bisection proof negate the indivisible part?
A) It shows that angles are finite
B) It shows that angles can be bisected infinitely, so no smallest part exists
C) It shows that straight lines cannot be divided
D) It shows that angles are not real

Key Takeaway
Euclid's bisection proof shows that any finite angle contains an infinite number of smaller angles, thereby refuting the existence of an indivisible spatial part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson proves that finite magnitudes contain infinite possibilities. How does this challenge your own mental tendency to reduce complex realities (like your faith, your character, or your relationships) into simple, manageable 'indivisible' units? What is one area where you have oversimplified something sacred, and what will you do today to restore its infinite depth?
?
The proof negates the existence of an indivisible part in the physical world. Yet your heart clings to an indivisible belief: the oneness of Allah. Have you allowed worldly pursuits to bisect your devotion, creating 'parts' of your attention? In the next 24 hours, how can you ensure your worship remains a coherent whole, not fragmented by distractions?
?
Euclid's argument relies on a process that never ends. Your journey towards Allah also has no endpoint in this life—each step of repentance opens new horizons. Are you tired of this infinite progression, or do you embrace it? What specific step of tawba or good deed will you add today to continue your own infinite bisection toward Him?

The Sixth Proof from Euclidean Line Division
Al-Jurjani presents Euclid's proof that any line is divisible, necessitating division of the assumed indivisible part.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Euclid's proof of line bisection undermines the concept of an indivisible part (al-juz' alladhi la yatajazza').

Core Idea
If a line can be bisected, so can any part containing the midpoint.

Al-Jurjani presents the sixth proof against the indivisible part, drawn from Euclid's Elements. This proof uses the well-known Euclidean demonstration that any line segment can be bisected. By assuming a line is composed of a finite number of indivisible parts, the bisection forces the middle part to divide, contradicting its indivisibility. Let's examine the logic closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the concise style—the entire proof is in one sentence.
2
Understand the Euclidean foundation
Recall that Euclid proved any line can be bisected; this is the key premise that makes the proof work.
This is a geometric truth taken as given.
3
Trace the reductio
Assume a line composed of, say, five indivisible parts. When the line is bisected, the midpoint falls inside the middle part, forcing that part to split.
4
Grasp the contradiction
The middle part would then be divisible, contradicting the assumption that all parts are indivisible.
This is the heart of the proof.
5
Reflect on broader significance
This proof shows that atomism (indivisible parts) leads to absurdity in geometry.
Consider why this refutation matters for kalam cosmology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه ( السادس : برهن ) إقليدس في تلك المقالة ( علي أن كل خط قابل للتنصيف، فإذا فرض ( الخط مركباً ) من أجزاء وتر كخمسة مثلاً ( لزم تجزؤ ) ( الجزء ( الوسطاني ) .
The sixth proof: Euclid proved in that article that every line is capable of bisection. So if a line is assumed to be composed of parts, such as five, then the middle part would necessarily divide.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage gives the sixth proof (al-wajh al-sadis) against the indivisible part, again from Euclid's Elements. Euclid proved that any line segment can be bisected. If we suppose a line is composed of a finite number of indivisible parts—say five—then the midpoint of the line would fall within the middle part. But since the line is divisible, that middle part would itself be divisible into two halves, contradicting its assumed indivisibility. Thus, no line can be composed of indivisible parts.

Key Terms
الخط
التنصيف
الجزء الوسطاني
المركب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof only works for an odd number of parts (like 5).
Correction: The proof works for any finite number of parts because the midpoint always falls in some part; that part (which may be middle in odd count, or one of the middle two in even count) must be divisible.

Checkpoint
In the sixth proof, what happens if a line is assumed to be composed of five indivisible parts?
A) The line cannot be bisected
B) The middle part would divide
C) The end parts would divide
D) The number of parts increases

Key Takeaway
Euclid's bisection proof shows that any part containing the midpoint of a line must itself be divisible, refuting the idea of an indivisible atomic part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, do you assume that some parts of your character are 'indivisible' and cannot be changed? How does this proof challenge your belief that some of your flaws are permanent and cannot be bisected by sincere effort and divine help?
?
This proof shows that even the middle part is divisible. What is the 'middle part' of your daily routine that you think is fixed but actually can be divided into moments of obedience and disobedience? Will you actively split that part today?
?
You just learned that a line, no matter how small its parts, can be divided. Do you apply this logic to your own heart? Are there 'indivisible' habits you claim you cannot break? What would it mean for you to accept that every spiritual flaw is divisible with God's permission?

The Objection to the Proof of Hayula and Its Answer
Objection to the proof of matter and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that matter's receptivity to connection and separation leads to an infinite regress, and how Al-Jurjani refutes it by showing that matter's unity and multiplicity depend on form, not on an inherent nature.

Core Idea
Matter is a pure disposition; its attributes come from form, not its essence.

Al-Jurjani presents a sophisticated objection against the proof of matter (hayula) from the philosophers, which claims that matter's receptivity to connection and separation would itself require an underlying matter, leading to an infinite regress. He then refutes it by clarifying that matter is not inherently qualified by connection or separation; rather, its unity and multiplicity come from the form that inheres in it. This passage is essential for understanding the nuanced debate on the composition of bodies in Islamic philosophy and kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the passage once to get the gist. Notice how the objector uses the same logic as the proof of hayula to argue that matter itself would need another matter.
The objection is a classic infinite regress argument.
2
Identify the key claim
The objector says that if matter is receptive to both connection and separation, then just as the body needed a matter, matter would need another matter, leading to regress. This is the core of the mu'arada.
3
See how the answer refutes it
Al-Jurjani's answer distinguishes between inherent and accidental attributes. Matter is not inherently connected or separated; its connection and separation come from the form that inheres in it. Therefore, no regress follows.
Focus on the phrase 'وإلا فهي في نفسها لا واحدة ولا كثيرة ولا متصلة ولا منفصلة'.
4
Reflect on the commentary
The commentary clarifies that the objection is better called a contradiction or refutation, and that matter's attributes are purely derivative from form.
The story of the candle is referenced as an analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The First Observatory - The Seventh Objective: The body is composed of matter and form. If its acceptance of both necessitated the proof of a matter) as you mentioned in the body (it would necessitate that matter have (another matter, then the discourse would transfer to it) and regress would follow) in ordered things existing together. (And it) i.e. this which was mentioned in the objection (is repelled) from them (by what we mentioned in the summary. For we proved that connection is not receptive (of alternating connection and separation, so no other matter is necessitated for matter) except by proving two things: one that it has a connection different from this connection which is an accident in it, so that it would be connected in its essence. (And the second: that it i.e. that different connection (disappears from it and returns to it, so that two things are established in the essence of matter: the different connection and what is receptive to it, so matter would have another matter) and that is not possible. For its unity i.e. the unity of matter (and its multiplicity are according to what happens to it from connection and what accompanies it from form. So before the occurrence of separation, it is one connected by the one form inhering in it, and after it, it becomes many separated by the multiple forms inhering in it. Otherwise, it) in itself (is not) one nor many nor connected nor separated; rather it) in its essence (is a disposition. His saying: (In the objection to their proof of matter, etc.) Some commentators said regarding its naming: This objection [is called] mu'arada is obscure; rather it is either a contradiction or a refutation. And in it there is that it does not engage with the premises specifically or generally. Rather it is explicit that your proof, even if it indicates the existence of matter, yet we have something that negates it, where he said: If this necessitated the proof of matter, regress would follow, for it is an argument contrary to what is desired. Its parts from one direction to another, and this occurs only by connection and separation; accordingly, the change of the corporeal form also follows. And we have already presented this investigation in the discussions of quantity at first, and its origin, which is the story of the candle, is mentioned in some philosophical books according to what is well-known. His saying: (And otherwise it in itself is not one nor many nor connected nor separated, etc.) means that matter becomes one by the unity of form, many by the multiplicity of form, connected by its connection, and separated by its separation. That [it is] a pure disposition, having no effect in the mentioned attributes (except through form), so it is qualified by them as a consequence [of form], not) in its essence.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is an objection (mu'arada) to the Proof of Matter (hayula) and its answer, followed by explanatory commentary. The objection states that if matter is one before division, it is connected; if many after division, it is separated; thus it is receptive of both connection and separation. If, as the proponents claim, this receptivity proves a matter underlying the body, then matter itself would require another matter to underlie its own connection and separation, leading to an infinite regress. The answer is that the connection they proved is not subject to alternating connection and separation; that would only require a second matter if one proves both that matter has a different connection inhering in it and that this different connection is removed and returns—neither of which can be proven. Instead, matter's unity and multiplicity depend on the connection and form that accompany it: before division, it is one and connected by the single form; after division, it becomes many and separated by multiple forms. In itself, matter is neither one nor many, neither connected nor separated; it is a pure disposition (isti'dad) with no active role in these attributes, which it receives through form as a consequence. The commentary then discusses the naming of the objection, clarifying that it is better described as a contradiction or refutation rather than a mere mu'arada, and notes that the argument does not address premises but presents a counter-argument. It also references the story of the candle and a discussion in the Physics (quantity). Finally, the commentary on 'And otherwise it in itself is not one nor many...' explains that matter acquires these attributes from form.

الانفصال
المعارضة
التسلسل
الاستعداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the objection is a valid refutation of the proof of matter, showing that matter leads to regress.
Correction: The answer shows that the objection fails because matter's attributes come from form, not its essence, so no regress actually follows.

Checkpoint
What does the objector claim would follow from accepting that matter is both connected and separated?
A) That connection and separation are accidental.
B) That matter would have another matter leading to regress.
C) That form is unnecessary.
D) That matter is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The objection fails because matter is a pure disposition; its unity, multiplicity, connection, and separation derive from the form, not from its own essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that matter's unity and multiplicity come from form, not from its own essence. Think of a time you felt fragmented by change. Did you mistake an accidental quality for your essential self? How can you anchor your identity in what is truly unchanging?
?
The objector assumed that receptivity to both connection and separation requires an underlying substrate, leading to regress. In your life, do you chase an infinite regress of explanations for your struggles, always looking for one more underlying cause? How can the answer—that attributes come from form, not substance—help you stop that regress and trust in a single, sufficient source?
?
Matter is a pure disposition, having no effect on its attributes except through form. Consider your own potential. Are you passive in shaping your form, or do you actively choose the forms (character, actions) that give you unity? What would it mean to take full responsibility for the form you bring to your life?

Refutation of Democritean Atomism
Al-Jurjani explains that the proof of hayula requires refuting atomism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the proof of matter (hayula) depends on a prior refutation of atomism, and what the atomist view entails.

Core Idea
The proof of matter cannot stand unless atomism is refuted first.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif introduces a crucial methodological move: before proving the existence of an underlying substance (hayula) that receives form, we must eliminate the atomist alternative. Al-Jurjani explains that the earlier proof is incomplete unless it first refutes the view of Democritus. Let's examine how atomism undermines the need for hayula and why it must be rejected.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to get a general sense of the argument. Do not worry about details yet.
The passage ends mid-sentence; that's fine for now.
2
Identify the atomist claim
Focus on the description of Democritus's view: what are the fundamental building blocks of bodies according to atomists? How do they explain connection and separation?
Note the key terms: 'أجزاء' (parts/atoms), 'متجزئة في الوهم' (divisible in imagination), 'غير قابلة للتجزئة بالفعل' (not actually divisible).
3
Understand the challenge to hayula
Reflect on why atomism, if true, would make the proof of a distinct underlying matter (hayula) unnecessary. What does atomism propose instead of hayula?
Atomism says bodies are just aggregates of atoms; there is no continuous substance that receives both connection and separation.
4
See the author's conclusion
Al-Jurjani states that the proof of hayula is not complete 'except by refuting the saying of those who say...' Understand that the proof depends on this refutation.
This is a methodological point: a proof must eliminate competing explanations to be valid.
5
Reflect on methodology
Consider why it is important for a theologian or philosopher to address alternative theories before building a positive argument. This is a common move in kalam.
The refutation of atomism is a necessary step, not an optional aside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن هذا البرهان ( الذي ذكر على إثبات الهيولى ( لا يتم إلا بإبطال قول من يقول : ( كديمقراطيس وأتباعه ) مبادئ الأجسام) البسيطة ( أجزاء ) هي أجسام صغار صلبة ( متجزئة في الوهم بحسب الجهات الثلاث، لكنها ( غير قابلة للتجزئة ) الموجبة للانفصال ( بالفعل) في الخارج ( واتصال الجسم) البسيط ( عبارة عن اجتماع تلك الأجزاء وانفصاله عن افتراقها وكل جزء منها متصل) في نفسه ( بالحقيقة وغير قابل للانفصال الانفكاكي، بل للانفصال الوهمي ( والجسم الذي يقبل الانفصال ) الفكي كالماء مثلا ( غير متصل ) في نفسه ( بالحقيقة ) بل بحس الحس لعجزه عن إدراك المفاصل التي بين تلك الأجزاء ) فليس ثمة أمر قابل للاتصال والانفصال ) بل هناك أجسام صغار تجتمع وتفترق ومحصول ما ذكره المصنف أن
And know that this proof (which was mentioned for the proof of matter (is not complete except by refuting the saying of those who say, (like Democritus and his followers,) that the principles of simple bodies (are parts) which are small, solid bodies (divisible in the imagination according to the three dimensions, but they (are not susceptible to division) which necessitates separation (actually) in the external world. (And the connection of a simple) body (is the aggregation of those parts and its separation is their dispersion, and each part is connected) in itself (in reality and not susceptible to disjunctive separation, but to imaginary separation. (And the body that accepts separation) such as water (is not connected) in itself (in reality) but by sense perception, due to its inability to perceive the joints between those parts. So there is no thing receptive to connection and separation, but there are small bodies that aggregate and disperse. And the sum of what the author mentioned is that
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a crucial clarification: the earlier proof of matter (hayula) is not complete unless it first refutes the atomist view of Democritus and his followers. Atomists hold that simple bodies are composed of indivisible atoms that are small, solid, and theoretically divisible only in imagination, not in actuality. For them, the connection of a simple body is merely the aggregation of these atoms, and its separation is their dispersion. Each atom is itself continuous in reality and not susceptible to physical division, only to imaginary division. A body that does undergo physical separation (like water) is not truly continuous in itself; rather, sense perception falsely perceives it as continuous because it cannot detect the gaps between the atoms. Thus, according to atomists, there is no underlying continuous substance that receives both connection and separation—only atoms that aggregate and disperse. The author then concludes that the sum of what the original author (al-Iji) mentioned is that... (the passage breaks off). The point is that if atomism were true, the proof of a separate matter (hayula) underlying bodies would be unnecessary, so the proof must first refute this view.

Key Terms
ديمقراطيس
الأجزاء
التجزئة
الانفصال الوهمي
إبطال القول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the proof of hayula is self-sufficient and does not need to address alternative theories.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the proof is not complete except by refuting the atomist view, showing that a proof must eliminate competing explanations.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what must be done before the proof of hayula can be considered complete?
A) Prove that atoms are indivisible.
B) Refute the atomist view of Democritus.
C) Show that connection and separation are accidents.
D) Establish the existence of form.

Key Takeaway
The proof of hayula is only valid after refuting atomism, because atomism accounts for change without a underlying substrate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm a belief, do you honestly engage with the strongest opposing view, or do you avoid it? This lesson shows that a proof is incomplete until its alternative is refuted. What belief do you hold that you have not yet tested against its counterargument? Will you take time to do that this week?
?
The atomists thought they explained change without a deeper substrate. In your spiritual life, do you settle for surface-level explanations (e.g., 'I just feel close to God') without examining the foundations of your faith? Where might you be avoiding the deeper work of intellectual scrutiny because it feels uncomfortable?
?
Your sense perception tells you that water is continuous, but the atomists argue it is actually discrete. In what areas of your life does your intuition deceive you? Are you willing to let revealed truth and reason correct your natural assumptions, even when it feels counterintuitive?

Hayula's Unity and Multiplicity Through Form
Al-Jurjani explains that hayula's unity and multiplicity depend on form, avoiding regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how matter (hayula) is neither one nor many in itself, and how form mediates these attributes, thereby avoiding an infinite regress.

Core Idea
Matter's unity and multiplicity come from form, not from itself.

Al-Jurjani delves into the nature of matter, addressing a subtle objection. This passage clarifies that matter's apparent unity or multiplicity is not intrinsic but derives from the forms that inhere in it. By understanding the role of form as an intermediary, we see why matter remains unchanged despite changing forms, preventing an infinite regression of substrates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the argument's flow. Notice the objection and response structure.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the objection
The hypothetical objection claims that matter's personal unity contradicts the statement that matter is not one in itself.
3
Understand the distinction
Al-Jurjani distinguishes between intrinsic personal unity (by which matter differs from celestial matter) and accidental unity/multiplicity from forms.
These two types of unity coexist.
4
Grasp the role of form
Form is the primary subject for attributes like unity and multiplicity; they occur to form first essentially, then to matter secondarily.
This prevents the need for another matter underlying matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإلا فهي في نفسها لا (واحدة أي وإن لا يعتبر معها الصورة الواحدة والمتعددة فهي في نفسها مسلوب عنها الوحدة والكثرة فإن قلت : هذا مناف لما تقرر عندهم من أن هيولى العناصر مع تكثرها بحسب الصورة النوعية للبسائط العنصرية والمواليد الثلاثة واحدة بالشخص والصورة المذكورة الواردة عليها لا تصير لوحدتها الشخصية كخشب واحد لونت بعضها بألوان مختلفة قلت : المراد أنه لا واحدة ولا متعددة بالوحدة والكثرة الحاصلتين من توارد الاتصالات ولها الوحدة الشخصية التي في نفسها بها يمتاز عن هيولى الأفلاك فهي ثابتة لها في حد ذاتها كسائر الموجودات الخارجية وتلك الوحدة تجامع الوحدة والكثرة المتواردتين عليها بحسب توارد الاتصاف .
ومعناه أن الصورة تكون واسطة في عروض هذه الأحوال للهيولى بحيث تكون هذه الأحوال عارضة للصورة أولاً، وبالذات وللهيولى ثانياً، وبالعرض وليس لشيء من هذه الأحوال عروضان متغايران يكون أحدهما للهيولى والآخر للصورة، بل كان هناك عروض واحد يكون للصورة أولاً وللهيولي ثانياً على ما ذكرنا آنفاً. نعم كانت الهيولى واسطة في ثبوت هذه الأحوال للمحل الحقيقي الذي هو الصورة ثم لا يذهب عليك أن الوحدة والاتصال هما لازمان لوجود الصورة قبل انقسام الجسم المتصل وأن الكثرة والاتصال هما لازمان لوجودها بعد انقسام الجسم المذكور، وأما الوجود والتشخص، فهما يكونان عارضين للهيولى بدون واسطة في العروض أصلاً وإن كان هناك واسطة في الثبوت أيضاً، فعلى هذا لا يلزم من تبدل وجودات الصور وتشخصاتها تبدل وجود الهيولى وتشخصها إذا المفروض أن الأحوال المذكورة أعني الوحدة وأخواتها لازمة لوجود الصورة وعارضة لها أولا وبالذات بخلاف الهيولى كما ذكرنا فحينئذ لا يلزم أن يكون للهيولى هيولى أخرى هذا هو الكلام اللائق بما هو المختار عندهم وقوله : لا فعل لها الفعل هاهنا هو ما يقابل القوة لا ما هو بمعنى التأثير كما يتوهم .
His saying: (And otherwise it in itself is not one) i.e. even if the single and multiple form is not considered with it, it is in itself negated of unity and multiplicity. If you say: This contradicts what is established with them that the matter of the elements, despite its multiplicity according to the specific form of elemental simples and the three kinds, is one in person, and the mentioned form that comes upon it does not make it lose its personal unity, like a single piece of wood whose parts are colored with different colors. I say: The intended meaning is that it is neither one nor multiple with the unity and multiplicity resulting from the succession of connections, and it has the personal unity that is in itself by which it is distinguished from the matter of the celestial spheres, so it is fixed for it in its essence like other external existents, and that unity coexists with the unity and multiplicity that succeed one another upon it according to the succession of qualification.
And its meaning is that form is an intermediary in the occurrence of these states to matter, such that these states occur to form first and essentially, and to matter secondarily and accidentally. And none of these states has two different occurrences, one for matter and the other for form; rather there is a single occurrence that is for form first and for matter second, as we mentioned earlier. Yes, matter is an intermediary in the subsistence of these states for the true subject which is form. Then do not overlook that unity and connection are necessary concomitants of the existence of form before the division of the connected body, and that multiplicity and separation are necessary concomitants of its existence after the division of the mentioned body. As for existence and individuation, they occur to matter without any intermediary in occurrence at all, even if there is an intermediary in subsistence also. Accordingly, from the change of the existences of forms and their individuations, it does not follow that the existence of matter and its individuation change, because the assumption is that the mentioned states, i.e. unity and its sisters, are necessary for the existence of form and occur to it first and essentially, unlike matter as we mentioned. Then no other matter is necessitated for matter. This is the appropriate speech according to what is chosen by them. And His saying: 'it has no effect'—'effect' here is what is opposed to potentiality, not what is in the sense of influence, as is imagined.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the phrase 'And otherwise it in itself is not one nor many...' from the earlier argument. It clarifies that hayula (matter) in its own essence is negated of unity and multiplicity; these attributes come from the form that inheres in it. A potential objection is raised: if matter is not one in itself, this contradicts the fact that the matter of all sublunary elements is one in person despite different forms (like a single piece of wood colored differently). The answer distinguishes two types of unity: the personal unity that matter possesses in itself (by which it is distinguished from celestial matter) and the accidental unity/multiplicity that comes from successive connections and forms. These two coexist. The commentary then explains that form serves as an intermediary: attributes like unity and multiplicity occur first to form essentially, then to matter secondarily. There is only one occurrence, not two. Matter is an intermediary in subsistence but not in occurrence. Unity and connection are necessary concomitants of form before division, and multiplicity and separation after division. Existence and individuation, however, occur to matter directly without intermediary in occurrence (though with an intermediary in subsistence). Therefore, the change of forms does not change matter's existence or individuation, and there is no need for another matter underlying matter. The passage concludes with a note on the term 'la fi'la laha' (it has no effect), explaining that 'fi'l' here means 'actuality' as opposed to potentiality, not 'influence'.

Key Terms
الوحدة الشخصية
توارد الاتصالات
العارض أولاً وبالذات
الوجود والتشخص
الفعل والقوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Matter possesses unity/multiplicity inherently.
Correction: The passage explains that unity and multiplicity are acquired through form; matter in itself is devoid of them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the role of form in the occurrence of unity and multiplicity to matter?
A) Form causes unity and multiplicity directly in matter.
B) Form is an intermediary: these states occur to form first, then to matter.
C) Form has no role; matter possesses these attributes inherently.
D) Form and matter each have separate occurrences of these attributes.

Key Takeaway
Matter's unity and multiplicity are not intrinsic but are derived from the forms that inhere in it, with form serving as the primary subject for these attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your identity feels shaped by your changing roles, achievements, and failures—your 'forms.' But this lesson teaches that your core self (like matter's personal unity) remains one and fixed. If that is true, why do you cling to external forms to define your worth? What would it take for you to ground your identity in Allah's constant regard rather than in transient attributes?
?
Al-Jurjani says that matter's personal unity distinguishes it from celestial matter—a distinction not self-made but given. Similarly, what distinguishes you from others is not your own doing. Does this truth humble you or frighten you? When you consider that your distinctiveness is a gift, how does that change the way you view your unique traits and responsibilities?
?
If you truly believed that your changing circumstances (forms) do not touch the depth of who you are (your personal unity), what would you dare to do differently tomorrow? Which fear would lose its grip if you knew that your core self is secure in Allah's hands, not subject to the flux of this world?

Objection to the Extended Substance and the Nature of the Dispute
Objection and answer about the denial of substantial extension.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the dispute over the extended substance and what the mutakallimun actually deny.

Core Idea
The dispute over extension is not about existence but about whether it is a real unitary thing.

In this passage, the author addresses a common objection: if many scholars deny the extended substance, how can it be the first perceived? The response reconfigures the debate, showing that the denial is not of extension per se but of certain accidental aspects. This clarifies the foundational starting point for arguments about body and substance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: comment, dismissal of a misunderstanding, objection, answer.
The translation is literal; some phrases may seem awkward.
2
Identify the objection
Find the sentence that begins 'It is said:' (قيل). This is the objection: how can the connected identity be the first perceived if many deny it?
3
Identify the answer
Find the answer starting with 'The answer is that' (أجيب بأنه). Notice how it reframes the dispute: it is not about existence of extension, but about whether it is one as perceived and whether it is the whole body.
The answer shifts the focus to what is really denied: accidental extensions (quantities).
4
Understand what is denied
The passage concludes that the mutakallimun and philosophers deny the accidental extensions (al-imtidadat al-^aradiyya), considering them non-existent because they are mere ends and discontinuities.
This clarifies that the substantial extension itself is not denied.
5
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters. It protects the claim that the extended substance is the first perceived and known necessarily, because the denial targets a different concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أي الجوهر الممتد في الجهات التي تثبت بنفي الجزء اتصاله في نفسه) فلا عبرة بما توهم من أن كون الاتصال جوهراً أو جزءاً من الجسم ظاهر البطلان إذ لا تعقل منه إلا ما يقابل الانفصال، وهما عرضان متفارقان على الجسم إذا تحققتهما كانا عائدين إلى وحدته وكثرته، وذلك لأن المراد بالاتصال هو الجرهر الممتد المتصل إلخ . بمعنى قوله : (بل هو الجسم في بادئ الرأي المعلوم وجوده بالضرورة قيل : إن الهوية الاتصالية الامتداد الجوهري مما أنكره المتكلمون وكثير من الفلاسفة فكيف يصح دعوى كونها أول ما يدركها وكونها معلوم الوجود بالضرورة وإنما ذلك هو المقادير والامتدادات العرضية أجيب بأنه نزاع في ثبوت جوهر مشابه الامتداد والاتصال وفي كونه مدركاً بالحس ولو بواسطة ما يقوم به من الأعراض، وإنما النزاع في أنه هل هو في نفس الأمر واحد كما هو عند الحس أم لا؟ وعلى الأول هل هو تمام الجسم أم لا ؟ بل يفتقر إلى جزء آخر يتوارد عليه الاتصال والانفصال والامتدادات العرضية أعني المقادير فهي التي أنكرها المتكلمون وكثير من الفلاسفة أعني القائلين بأنها أمور عدمية لكونها نهايات وانقطاعات .
His saying: (i.e. the extended substance in the directions whose connection in itself is proven by negating the part) So no regard is given to the supposition that connection being a substance or a part of the body is clearly invalid, because nothing is understood from it except what is opposed to disconnection, and they are two accidental (^arad) properties on the body; if you realize them, they return to its unity and multiplicity. That is because the intended meaning of connection is the extended, connected substance etc. In the sense of his saying: (Rather it is the body in the first view, known necessarily to exist.) It is said: 'The connected identity, the substantial extension, is something denied by the speculative theologians (mutakallimun) and many philosophers. So how can the claim that it is the first perceived and known necessarily be valid? Rather that is the quantities and accidental extensions.' The answer is that the dispute is about the existence of a substance similar to extension and connection, and about its being perceived by sense, albeit through the accidents that subsist in it. Rather the dispute is whether it is in reality one as it is at sense or not? And on the first view, is it the whole body or not? Rather it needs another part upon which connection, disconnection, and accidental extensions, i.e. quantities, occur. These are what the speculative theologians and many philosophers denied, meaning those who say they are non-existent things because they are ends and discontinuities.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. It begins by clarifying a line: 'i.e. the extended substance...' and dismisses the misunderstanding that connection as a substance or part is obviously false, explaining that connection is understood only as opposed to disconnection, both being accidents that relate to unity and multiplicity. The objection itself is then presented: some say that the connected identity and substantial extension are denied by mutakallimun and many philosophers, so how can it be claimed that it is the first perceived and known necessarily? The answer is that the dispute is not about the existence of a substance akin to extension per se, but about whether it is really one as perceived, whether it is the whole body or needs another part to receive connection and disconnection. The quantities and accidental extensions (al-maqadir wa al-imtidadat al-^aradiyya) are what the mutakallimun deny, considering them non-existent as they are merely ends and cuts. Thus the objection is answered by re-framing the point of contention.

Key Terms
المتكلمون (mutakallimun)
الهوية الاتصالية (connected identity)
الامتداد الجوهري (substantial extension)
المقادير (quantities)
الامتدادات العرضية (accidental extensions)
الحس (sense)
العرض (accident)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the mutakallimun and philosophers completely deny the extended substance or that extension is not real at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the denial is only about the accidental extensions (quantities) as real entities, not about the substantial extension itself.

Checkpoint
What do the mutakallimun and many philosophers deny according to the answer in this passage?
A) The existence of any extension
B) The accidental extensions (al-imtidadat al-^aradiyya) as being real entities
C) The extended substance itself
D) The perception of dimensions

Key Takeaway
The mutakallimun do not deny extension itself; they deny that the accidental extensions (quantities) are real entities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that the dispute about extension is not about existence but about its true reality. Be honest: in your daily life, do you often argue about the 'existence' of things—like whether an event really happened—while ignoring the deeper question of what that event actually means for your soul? What would it take for you to shift your focus from surface disagreements to the reality of your relationship with Allah?
?
The mutakallimun denied accidental extensions because they are mere ends and discontinuities—not real in themselves. Think about the goals and possessions you chase: your career milestones, your social status, your next achievement. If you truly recognized them as 'accidental extensions'—temporary and ultimately non-existent—how would your priorities change starting today?
?
The substance is perceived through its accidents, but the reality behind it is one. When you look at your own life—your successes, failures, sins, and good deeds—do you see only a collection of disconnected events, or do you perceive the one continuous soul that stands before Allah? What one habit could you establish this week to help you see your life as a unified whole accountable to Him?

6 min
When Connection as a Part Eliminates Receptivity to Disconnection
Presents a logical objection against connection as a part, with counter-objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical contradiction that arises if connection is considered a part of the body while the body is simultaneously receptive to disconnection.

Core Idea
If connection is a part, its removal annihilates the body, so the body cannot be receptive to that removal.

This lesson presents a sharp logical objection against the view that connection (ittisal) is a part of the body. If connection were a part, then disconnection (the removal of connection) would destroy the whole body, making the body unable to receive disconnection. Yet proponents of the view also claim the body is receptive to disconnection. The objection shows that these two claims cannot coexist without contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Understand the background claim
Recall that some scholars hold that the connected substance is the reality of the body and that connection is a part of it.
2
Identify the objection's structure
The objection argues: if connection is a part, then its removal (disconnection) destroys the whole, so the body is not receptive to disconnection. But the body is claimed to be receptive—so contradiction.
Notice this is a classic reductio ad absurdum.
3
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Focus on the logical move from premise to contradiction.
The passage also includes a counter-objection about educational quantity, but the main point is the contradiction.
4
Reflect on the counter-objection
Consider the suggested way out: perhaps connection belongs to the educational quantity essentially, not to the connected substance. Does this resolve the contradiction?
The passage leaves this open.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جوهراً وراء هذا الجوهر المتصل، لكن المشهور أنه يقول : إن هذا الجوهر المتصل قائم بنفسه وهو حقيقة الجسم ومحل للاتصال الذي هو الوحدة والانفصال الذي هو الكثرة على معنى أنهما عرضان يحلان فيه على التعاقب كما ذهب إليه أفلاطون من أن آخر ما تنحل إليه الأجسام هو هذا الجوهر المتصل الممتد في الجهات كلها فطريق الرد عليه أنه يلزم من ذلك أن يكون التفريق إعداماً للجسم بالكلية وإيجاداً لقسمين آخرين من كتم العدم وهو باطل كما سيأتي تحقيقه ) وهاهنا سؤال يستصعبه بعض و ) ذلك السؤال ( هو أن الاتصال إذا كان جزءا للجسم كما زعمتم ( فبزواله ) الذي الانفصال ( تعدم هوية الجسم لانتفاء الكل بانتفاء جزئه ( فلا يكون الجسم قابلاً له ) أي لزواله أعني الانفصال ( وإذا كان الجسم ( قابلاً لزواله كما ادعيتموه أيضاً، فلا بد أن ( يبقى مع زواله) وإذا بقي معه فليس هو أي الاتصال ( جزءاً للجسم) والحاصل أن كون الجسم قابلاً للانفصال الذي هو زوال الاتصال ينافي كون الاتصال جزءاً له، فقد لزمكم فيما ذهبتم إليه القول باجتماع المتنافيين . (وظن) المستصعب (أن هو قوله : (ما تنحل إليه (الأجسام المركبة . قوله : ( كما زعمتم ) حيث قلتم : إن هذا الاتصال ليس تمام حقيقة الجسم . قوله: (والحاصل إلخ) في شرح المقاصد أن كون الاتصال جزءاً من الجسم ينافي كونه قابلاً للاتصال والانفصال، لأن الأول يستلزم الجسم عند زوال الاتصال، والثاني يستلزم بقاءه عنده ضرورة اجتماع القابل مع المقبول، فحينئذ يتوجه أن يقال : لو كان الاتصال جزءاً وقد قلتم بحصة الملزوم .انتهى. وهذا التقرير يشعر بأن السؤال المذكور معارضة في المقدمة. إما في مقدمة أن الاتصال جزء من الجسم أو في مقدمة أن الجسم قابل للانفصال وتقرير الشارح يدل على أنه نقض لبرهان الهيولى باستلزامه المحال . قوله : ( فيما ذهبتم إليه أي في الاستدلال الذي ذهبتم إليه . قوله : أنه يلزم من (ذلك أي يلزم من كون الجوهر المتصل حقيقة الجسم أن يكون التفريق إعداماً للجسم بالكلية لكن يتوجه عليه أنه يجوز أن يكون الاتصال والوحدة ونحوهما، أموراً ثابتة للكم المسمى التعليمي أولاً وبالذات وللجوهر المتصل ثانياً وبالعرض، فلم يلزم من ذلك أن يكون التفريق إعداماً للجسم بالكلية فإن هذه الأمور لازمة للجسم التعليمي لا لوجود الجوهر المتصل كما زعمتم ثم إنه يمكن توجيه هذه المناقشة على ما يذكر فيما بعد أيضاً من قوله : وكيف يكون الواحد بالشخص واحداً تارة إلخ ؟ وعلى ما يذكر بعد ذلك أيضاً من قوله : ولا شك أنه الجوهر المتصل الواحد آني ليس باقياً. قوله : ( وهاهنا سؤال إلخ) ولعل هذا السؤال جعل نقضاً إجمالياً باستلزام الدليل المذكور محالاً، وذلك المحال هو إجماع المتنافيين كما بينه .
A substance beyond this connected substance, but the well-known (view) is that he says: This connected substance is self-subsistent, and it is the reality of the body and the locus for connection which is unity and for disconnection which is multiplicity, meaning that they are two accidents inhering in it successively, as Plato held: the ultimate resolution of bodies is this connected substance extended in all directions. The way to refute it is that it would follow from that that division is a complete annihilation of the body and a bringing into existence of two other parts from the concealment of non-existence, which is false, as will be verified later. And here there is a question that some find difficult, and that question is: If connection is a part of the body as you claim, then with its removal, which is disconnection, the identity of the body is annihilated because the whole is annihilated by the annihilation of its part, so the body would not be receptive to it, i.e. to its removal, i.e. disconnection. And if the body is receptive to its removal, as you also claim, then it must remain with its removal; and if it remains with it, then connection is not a part of the body. The conclusion is that the body being receptive to disconnection, which is the removal of connection, contradicts connection being a part of it. So you are compelled in your position to affirm the conjunction of two contradictories. (And the one who finds it difficult thought that...) His saying: (what composite bodies resolve into). His saying: (as you claimed) where you said that this connection is not the complete reality of the body. His saying: (and the conclusion etc.) in Sharh al-Maqasid: That connection being a part of the body contradicts its being receptive to connection and disconnection, because the first entails the body at the removal of connection, and the second entails its persistence with it due to the necessity of the conjunction of the receptive with the received. Then it follows that it should be said: If connection were a part, and you have said by the portion of the necessary consequence... end. And this presentation indicates that the mentioned question is a contradiction in the premise, either in the premise that connection is a part of the body or in the premise that the body is receptive to disconnection. And the commentator's presentation indicates that it is a refutation of the proof of hyle (hayula) by entailing an impossibility. His saying: (in what you have held to) i.e. in the proof you have held to. His saying: that it follows from that, i.e. it follows from the connected substance being the reality of the body that division is a complete annihilation of the body, but it can be objected that it is possible that connection, unity, and the like are things that belong to the quantity called al-ta^limi first and essentially, and to the connected substance secondarily and accidentally; so it does not follow that division is a complete annihilation of the body, because these things are necessary for the educational body (jism ta^limi), not for the existence of the connected substance as you claimed. Then it is possible to direct this discussion to what will be mentioned later also from his saying: 'How can the one in person be one at one time etc.?' And to what will be mentioned after that also from his saying: 'And there is no doubt that the one connected substance in the moment is not remaining.' His saying: (and here there is a question etc.) Perhaps this question was made as a summary refutation by entailing that the mentioned proof entails an impossibility, and that impossibility is the conjunction of two contradictories as he explained.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents a major objection (sual) to the claim that connection (ittisal) is a part of the body. It begins by recounting the position of those who hold that the connected substance is self-subsistent and the reality of the body, serving as a locus for connection (unity) and disconnection (multiplicity) as accidents. The refutation of that view is noted: division would annihilate the body and create new parts from non-existence. Then the difficult question is stated: if connection is a part, its removal (disconnection) would destroy the body entirely, so the body cannot be receptive to disconnection; but if it is receptive (as claimed), then it must remain after disconnection, so connection is not a part. These two are contradictory. The commentary then explains that this question is a contradiction of premises: either connection is not a part or the body is not receptive to disconnection. It references Sharh al-Maqasid for further clarification. The passage concludes with a potential counter-objection: that connection and unity might belong to the 'educational quantity' (al-kamm al-ta^limi) essentially and to the connected substance only accidentally, thus avoiding the annihilation. This counter-objection is noted but not fully resolved here; the passage ends by suggesting the question is a summary refutation showing the proof implies a contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that connection and receptivity to disconnection are compatible without contradiction.
Correction: If connection is a part, its removal destroys the whole; thus the body cannot be receptive to that removal. Claiming both leads to the fallacy of affirming contradictories.

Checkpoint
What does the question (sual) aim to show about the view that connection is a part of the body?
A) That it is obviously true
B) That it leads to a contradiction
C) That it agrees with Plato
D) That it is supported by Sharh al-Maqasid

Key Takeaway
The objection shows that claiming connection is a part of the body while also affirming the body's receptivity to disconnection leads to a logical contradiction, undermining the view that connection is a part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a theological belief, do you ever test it for internal contradictions? Or do you avoid that because it might be unsettling? What would it mean for your faith if you found a contradiction in your own reasoning?
?
This passage shows the importance of accepting the logical consequences of one's premises. Are there any beliefs you cling to without having fully thought through their implications? Would you be willing to re-examine them if a contradiction was pointed out?
?
The scholar notes that some find this question difficult. When you encounter a difficult argument that challenges your understanding, do you lean into the difficulty or dismiss it? What does your response reveal about your intellectual humility and love for truth?
